Emergency and External Assistance Work of the Flood Relief Committee 112

The National Government Flood Relief Committee issued the following announcements regarding emergency and external assistance work: (1) The National Government Flood Relief Committee officially announced that regarding the request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to telegraph the U.S. Department of Agriculture to purchase wheat at a low price, it has received a reply from the United States that the matter is under consideration. (2) The Flood Relief Committee announced that the committee received a telegram from the Health Section of the League of Nations stating that it intends to send disease prevention experts from the health bureaus of India, the Netherlands East Indies, and Japan to China to assist in disease prevention work in the disaster areas. These experts will specialize in handling health matters in the disaster areas and will cooperate fully with various health agencies. The committee has replied by telegram agreeing. (3) The Flood Relief Committee is currently planning to charter ships to transport refugees out of the disaster areas and to transport food and other supplies to the disaster areas. In addition to chartering ships in Shanghai, it has also agreed with the military authorities to release five ships and ten small ships detained in Jiujiang for the committee's transportation use. The committee also received a telegram from engineer Baker requesting the urgent dispatch of ships to rescue refugees on the Jiujiang and Anqing dikes. The committee has acted accordingly.

Yesterday's News from the Provincial Flood Relief Fundraising Associations 113

▲The Fundraising Group Held Its First Meeting Yesterday

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Provincial Flood Relief held its first meeting of the Fundraising Group at 4:00 pm yesterday at Renji Hall. Attendees included Huang Renzhi, Zhang Gongquan, Li Zuyu, Wu Jingxiong, Wang Xiaolai, He Dekui, Wu Zhihao, Lin Kanghou, Qian Longzhang, Gui Yanfang, Tao Leqin, Jin Houcheng, Zhang Yichen, Xu Yongzuo, Wang Boyuan, Hu Xisheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhu Buqing, Jin Guanfu, Xiang Songmao, Zhu Zengyu, Yu Zhongxian, and Sheng Zhenlan. Huang Renzhi chaired the meeting. The discussion is summarized below:

▲Conveners Convened Yesterday The conveners designated yesterday included Jin Guanfu for the General Affairs Group, Zhang Gongquan for the Finance Group, Zhang Zhuping for the Propaganda Group, Li Zuyu for the Design Group, Wu Zhihao for the Fundraising Group, Zhang Zhijiang and Qu Yingguang for the Relief Group, Xiang Songmao for the Medicine Delivery Group, and Wen Lanting for the Auditing Group.

▲Organizational Charter The organizational charter was amended as follows: Article 1: All those who are enthusiastic about charity and support the Association's fundraising for emergency relief are members of the Association. Article 2: The members of the Association shall elect several executive committee members, and the executive committee shall jointly elect eleven standing committee members, six finance committee members, and four secretaries-general to handle the Association's affairs. Article 3: The meetings of the Association are as follows: (1) General meeting, held once a month; (2) Standing committee meeting, held once a week; (3) Extraordinary meetings may be convened in case of emergencies. Article 4: The Association shall establish the following groups to handle affairs: A. General Affairs Group: in charge of documents, accounting, general affairs, receiving and dispatching, recording, reporting, and matters not belonging to other groups. B. Design Group: in charge of planning, fundraising, donations, and relief matters. C. Fundraising Group: in charge of implementing fundraising for various donations, relief funds, and relief supplies. D. Finance Group: in charge of receiving relief funds and relief supplies, storing, remitting, and purchasing matters. E. Propaganda Group: in charge of compiling disaster reports and publicity matters. F. Relief Group: in charge of investigating distribution and matters related to agricultural and industrial relief and transportation. G. Medical Group: in charge of storing medicines, treating diseases, preventing epidemics, and all health matters. H. Auditing Group: in charge of auditing relief funds and relief supplies and the Association's income and expenditure. Each group shall hold at least two group meetings per week. In the event of related matters, joint meetings of the groups may be convened. The resolutions of the group meetings and joint meetings shall be reported to the standing committee. The operating procedures of each group shall be determined separately. Article 5: Each of the groups in the preceding article shall have a chairman, who shall be publicly elected by the standing committee. The number of chairmen shall be determined according to the complexity of the affairs. Each group may have several secretaries, who shall be recommended by the chairman and appointed by the standing committee. Article 6: All members, committee members, secretaries, and chairmen are volunteers. If it is deemed necessary to pay salaries or allowances to secretaries, the standing committee shall determine the amount. Employees may be hired for drawing documents, charts, and telecommunications, and salaries shall be paid at the discretion of the standing committee. Article 7: This charter shall be implemented from the date of establishment of the Association.

▲Discussion on Fundraising Yesterday, during the discussion on fundraising, in addition to the General Affairs Group reporting on the resolutions of the first general meeting, Wu Zhihao, Li Zuyu, Wang Laixiao, Wu Jingxiong, Tao Leqin, He Dekui, and others successively expressed their opinions. They all spoke passionately about the widespread devastation in the provinces and advocated for immediate fundraising and the rapid determination of various fundraising methods. As a result, the chairman summarized three principles: (1) requesting assistance from government agencies, (2) requesting fundraising from trade associations, and (3) general fundraising methods. All were approved one by one. At that time, Wang Xiaogao, Yu Zhongxian, Zheng Chengqing, Qian Longzhang, Zhang Yichen, Tao Leqin, Wu Zhihao, Wu Jingxiong, Qin Runqing, Xu Yongzuo, and Lin Kanghou were immediately designated as members of the trade association fundraising group, to be convened by Wang Xiaolai to start work immediately and report the detailed measures within three days. In addition, Gui Yanfang's proposal to issue more donation books to widely conduct fundraising was also passed.

▲The Propaganda Committee Was Established Yesterday

The Shanghai Provincial Flood Relief Fundraising Association previously invited Mr. Zhang Zhuping to organize the Relief Association Propaganda Committee. Mr. Zhang submitted it to the Daily Newspaper Association for discussion, and the association fully agreed. Mr. Zhang then hosted a banquet at Jue Lin Vegetarian Restaurant on Wangping Street yesterday afternoon, inviting representatives from various newspapers, news agencies, and advertising companies in Shanghai to discuss the implementation of the Propaganda Committee. A charter was approved on the spot, and secretaries of various groups were elected. The Propaganda Committee of the Flood Relief Fundraising Association was formally established yesterday. The details are summarized below:

▲Participating Representatives The representatives of various newspapers, news agencies, and advertising companies who participated yesterday, in addition to Mr. Zhang Zhuping himself, included Yu Daxiong, Zhu Zunyu, Sun Choucheng, Xu Xinyi, Zheng Yaonan, Zhang Zhihan, Ma Yinliang, Zhu Yixin, Chen Binhe, Zhou Kaijia, Huang Renzhi, Wang Zilian, Wang Boqi, Pan Gongbi, Dong Xianguang, Lin Zhenbin, as well as Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Affairs Committee, and Jin Guanfu, Secretary.

▲Discussion The representatives arrived and elected Mr. Huang Renzhi as chairman, reported the purpose of the meeting, and discussed the Propaganda Committee charter. Then, they elected committee members and passed the charter. Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Affairs Committee, gave a speech, stating that the establishment of this Relief Association Propaganda Committee was due to the efforts of Mr. Zhang Zhuping and the support of the news industry. He, as a fellow countryman, briefly stated that the establishment of this Propaganda Committee was "the gospel for disaster victims". Zhang Zhuping and others then proposed a propaganda plan, and the meeting adjourned.

▲Propaganda Plan Five propaganda plans were discussed yesterday: (1) For newspapers, provide information to newspapers, select commentaries, solicit disaster information from various places, and fundraising methods; (2) For advertising, ask advertising companies to solicit donations from all sectors of society for newspaper advertisements and roadside posters in various places for publicity; (3) For communications, news agencies will use telegrams and communications to publish in various places; (4) For publicity materials, such as leaflets, distribute them in Shanghai and other places; (5) Other aspects, such as showing disaster conditions in theaters and cinemas, and organizing performing arts groups.

▲Election of Secretaries Yesterday, the following were elected as secretaries: Shi Liangcai, Zhang Zhuping, Wang Boqi, Wang Zilian, and Zheng Yaonan as finance secretaries; Dong Xianguang, Zhou Kaijia, Zhu Yixin, Lin Zhenbin, and Huang Renzhi as design secretaries; Wang Yingbin, Wang Zhongwei, Pan Gongbi, Ma Yinliang, Ren Jinpin, Xu Xinyi, Yu Daxiong, Wu Lingyuan, Chen Binhe, Zhang Zhihan, Zhu Zunyu, Sun Choucheng, Zhu Yongkang, Yan Duhe, and National News Agency (to be handled by Mr. Zhang Zhuping) as standing committee members; Ren Jinpin as resident secretary.

▲Finance Meeting After the meeting adjourned, a meeting of the secretaries of each group was held at the Daily Newspaper Association. The finance secretaries decided that all propaganda expenses would be the responsibility of secretaries Shi, Zhang, Wang, and Zheng, and each would advance 100 yuan, totaling 500 yuan, as the Propaganda Committee's expenses. All subsequent expenses would not be raised from the outside world, and the expenses of the resident secretary would be borne by the Daily Newspaper Association. In addition, each newspaper would send one person to help with the propaganda work. All propaganda materials that could be printed by the newspaper would be printed by the newspaper, and if they could not be printed, other methods would be found to obtain voluntary printing from various parties.

▲Joint Meeting In addition to the finance secretaries, regarding advertising, Wang Zilian, Zheng Yaonan, and Lin Zhenbin would separately convene a meeting of the Advertising Association to discuss the implementation methods. In addition, the design secretaries and the current affairs secretaries also held a joint meeting yesterday, deciding on six implementation procedures: (1) interviewing, recording, and issuing manuscripts, (2) collecting, writing, and documenting, (3) statistics, affairs, and communication, (4) photography, drawing, printing, typesetting, and films, (5) advertising, and (6) lectures and performances. All of the above matters would be determined by the committee members and carried out separately.

▲Standing Committee Today At 3:00 pm today, the standing committee secretaries will convene another meeting to discuss all implementation guidelines.

▲Sending Personnel to Wuhan The disaster situation throughout the country is most severe in Wuhan. After the establishment of the Relief Association Propaganda Committee yesterday, the National Government Flood Disaster Committee sent personnel by plane to Wuhan today to investigate the disaster situation. The Propaganda Group considered the investigation to be very important, so yesterday, Mr. Zhang Zhuping specially sent Shenbao photographer Li Ziyang to Wuhan to investigate, take photographs, and communicate.

▲Approved Charter (1) This Propaganda Committee is organized by three representatives from each newspaper, news agency, and advertising company in Shanghai, and external personnel may be hired to join at any time. (2) All propaganda matters of the Shanghai Flood Relief Fundraising Association for the provinces will be managed by this committee. (3) The propaganda expenses required by this committee will be raised by itself, without raising funds from all sectors of society and without using public funds. (4) This association shall appoint five finance secretaries to be responsible for the fundraising of propaganda expenses, five design secretaries to plan the progress of this association, fifteen executive secretaries to preside over the affairs of this association, and designate one resident secretary to handle affairs permanently. (5) This committee shall meet every Thursday at 12:30 noon, and the meeting shall end at 2:30 pm. When necessary, extraordinary meetings may be convened. Standing executives and other committee members of the Relief Association may be invited to attend and provide guidance. (6) Each key member of this committee shall hold a meeting each week, and the time shall be determined by themselves. (7) This association may hire a number of staff members as needed in fact. (8) If there are any matters not covered in this charter, they may be amended by the decision of this committee.

Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Standing Committee Meeting 114

▲ Ordered Flour for Distribution

▲ Appointed Directors for Investigation and Distribution

The Jiangsu Flood Relief Association held its first standing committee meeting yesterday. Attendees included committee members Wang Bin'yan, Wen Lanting, Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Cheng Jingsheng, Wang Xiaolai, and Weng Yinchu, among others. (Reports Made): (1) Disaster reports from various counties in the form of letters and telegrams; (2) Hiring specialists to conduct surveys in different areas and prepare temporary relief measures; (3) Sending additional letters to the Relief Affairs Association for donation registers; (4) Fan Fayuan proposed reducing meals to aid relief efforts, suggesting a reduction of four-tenths of the daily food expenses each month to promote this idea. Additionally, Manager Fan's Hua Fa Construction Company offered to donate 10% of the daily sales of golden ear mushrooms to relief efforts; (5) Receiving relief donations (remainder omitted). Matters for discussion and resolution: (1) Appointing heads and deputy heads of each section, as well as staff; (2) Approving detailed regulations for investigation and distribution; (3) Approving detailed working regulations; (4) Approving the advance purchase of 20,000 bags of flour for distribution; (5) Considering the request by gentleman Jiang Zhongxiang for subsidies to the Red Swastika Society for joint temporary relief of Jiangpu refugees; it was resolved to send a telegram to Commissioner Qiao to handle the matter appropriately; (6) Co-organizing with Jisheng Society in Siyang, Huaiyin, and Huai'an, adding the Jisheng Society's chop to documents; (7) Telegram to the Ministry of Transportation requesting the printing of telegraph paper; (8) Appointing directors for investigation and distribution (remainder omitted). Appointed staff for the administrative team: (Head of Auditing Section) Wang Mingji, (Staff) Zhu Qi; (Head of Documentation Section) Wu Qijie, (Staff) Cheng Jianxun; (Head of Accounting Section) Weng Yinchu, Deputy Head Chen Shirui, (Staff) Zhang Zixin; (Head of General Affairs Section) Shi Peihou, (Staff) Wu Siyuan, Zhang Shudu. Appointed directors for investigation and distribution: Wang Huai, Liu Zhongzhuo, Qiao Baoyuan, Zhu Qijun, Hao Jifu, Chen Borong, Zhang Zhongkuan, Li Yushu, Cao Songqiao, Wu Peng, Song Deyi, Yuan Jimei. Summary of Investigation and Distribution Regulations: Relief standards prioritize disaster relief over poverty alleviation, strictly exclude secondary disasters, prioritize urgent households for distribution, and require investigators to personally visit disaster areas and issue vouchers by hand. Investigators are not responsible for money; funds are managed by local governments and public organizations and distributed publicly to disaster victims upon presentation of vouchers. Public announcements must be made in advance, specifying the amount of money, so that the public is aware. Vouchers will be used for reimbursement in the future. Prohibitions for investigators: (1) Prohibit inexperienced personnel who cannot distinguish disaster victims or prevent fraud, resulting in misallocation of relief funds; (2) Prohibit shirking responsibility by relying on official requests to have officials conduct household surveys on their behalf; (3) Prohibit biased opinions from local figures, leading to improper assessment of disaster severity; (4) Prohibit not personally visiting disaster areas and instead relying on village heads; (5) Prohibit accepting food and drink or any other provisions from local gentry and people; (6) Prohibit acting impulsively and refusing to listen humbly and seek detailed information from disaster victims; (7) Prohibit being soft-hearted and considering minor disasters as extreme poverty, leading to indiscriminate distribution of relief vouchers; (8) Prohibit perfunctory performance of duties; (9) Prohibit arbitrary delays; (10) Prohibit disharmony among colleagues, hindering progress.

Sino-Foreign Relief Association Actively Provides Relief to Flood Victims in Various Provinces 115

▲ Distributing Relief Funds

The Shanghai Sino-Foreign Relief Association, recognizing the severity of floods in various provinces, especially the exceptionally tragic situation in Hankou, which has not seen such a disaster since the Daoguang 29th year (1849), has been holding emergency meetings for several days. The Chinese and Western directors present, including Western directors Father Raoul de Jaegher, Mr. Benazet, Mr. Meyerkort (Manager of Citibank), and Chinese directors Song Hantong, Lu Weiyong, Zhang Xianqing, Zhu Yinjiang, Sun Zhongying, Chen Liangyu, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Junsheng, Jing Runshi, Yan Chengde, Lu Bohong, and Gu Jisheng, all expressed deep concern over the vastness of the disaster areas and the difficulty of raising relief funds. They decided to establish a fundraising committee urgently while immediately allocating available relief funds, prioritizing severely affected areas in northern Anhui and northern Jiangsu with 10,000 yuan each, selecting the most in need for distribution. However, the relief funds were limited. Fortunately, Chinese directors present raised 22,000 yuan on the spot, specifically for rescuing Hankou residents struggling in the flood.

Ningbo and Shaoxing Compatriots in Shanghai Raise Funds to Rescue Hankou Flood Victims 116

▲ Hua Wu Steamship Fully Loaded with Food Set to Sail for Hankou Today

The Hankou flood is exceptionally severe, and flood victims are in urgent need of rescue. The Ningbo Compatriot Association in Shanghai, the Shaoxing Seven Counties Compatriot Association in Shanghai, and the Shanghai Siming Public Hall held a meeting yesterday at the Ningbo Compatriot Association to address this matter. Attendees included Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Yongni, Yuan Ludeng, Fang Jiaobo, Sun Meitang, Xiang Songmao, Wu Zhihao, Ge Yuchen, and over forty others. They spent the entire day discussing ways to assist compatriots in Hankou and resolved to establish a Ningbo-Shaoxing Hankou Disaster Relief Association. In addition to sending telegrams requesting the General Headquarters Transportation Department to order the Yongxing steamship currently in military service to proceed to Hankou, and instructing the Xin Ningxing steamship stationed in Hankou to provide as much assistance as possible, they also chartered the Hua Wu steamship, with a capacity of over 7,000 tons, to transport 5,000 bags of flour, over 500 stones of rice, hundreds of boxes of biscuits, and all necessary medical supplies, which will set sail on the 21st. The Ningbo Compatriot Association has designated Mao Heyuan, Hong Xuefan, Dong Xinqin, Qiu Changfu, Chen Yuansheng, Dai Songnian, Xu Yunguan, Yao Youbao, and others to handle matters on board. They have also invited German medical doctor Xie Qigang to serve as the physician. The Shaoxing Seven Counties Compatriot Association has designated Lu Zhinan, Weng Yunhe, Yu Futian, Wei Hongwen, and others. Additionally, there will be a twelve-member escort team provided by the Ningbo-Shaoxing Company.

Page 14

All matters in Hankou have been entrusted to Yin Huichang and Zhang Yanling, managers of the Siming Bank, with full authority. Attached below are copies of the telegrams: "Telegram 1" To Director Qiu and Director Lai of the Transportation Department, Nanjing General Headquarters: The Hankou flood has reached the upper floors. Ningbo and Shaoxing compatriots are in dire need. In addition to telegraphing the Xin Ningxing and Yongxing ships in Hankou to provide as much assistance as possible, the number of ships is insufficient. Request that you promptly dispatch the Yongxing steamship currently in military service to Hankou immediately to coordinate assistance with the Ningbo and Shaoxing Compatriot Associations. Awaiting your telegraphic reply. "Telegram 2" To Chairman He in Hankou: The disaster in Hankou is exceptionally severe. Ningbo and Shaoxing compatriots are in dire need. We have already telegraphed the Xin Ningxing steamship in Hankou to provide as much assistance as possible. Concerned about potential disturbances due to large crowds, please promptly instruct the military police to maintain order. "Telegram 3" To the Sanbei Office in Hankou, and Ningbo, Shaoxing Compatriot Associations, and Siming Public Hall: The flood has reached the upper floors. We have agreed that the Xin Ningxing will transport compatriots and flood victims exclusively, free of charge for those unable to pay, directly to Ningbo. Please coordinate."

Further news: The Minister of Transportation, Mr. Song, telegraphed the Inspector General of Customs to instruct the Jianghai and Jianghan Customs to waive taxes and allow the Hua Wu steamship transporting food and medicine to Hankou to proceed. The Jisheng Society will be responsible for relief matters, the Red Cross for sanitation, and the Ningbo and Shaoxing compatriot organizations for reception duties. However, due to the vastness of the disaster area, disturbances are feared. Yu Qiaqing and Zhang Yongni telegraphed Chairman He, Commander Xia, and Superintendent Xu, stating: "The disaster in Hankou is exceptionally severe. The Ningbo-Shaoxing Compatriots have established an emergency relief association to rescue compatriots in Hankou and have dispatched the Xin Ningxing, Yongxing, and Hua Wu steamships to Hankou for assistance. We have entrusted Mr. Yin Dongchang to be stationed in Hankou and take charge. In addition to Mr. Yin presenting the details in person, we respectfully request that you acknowledge and coordinate, and provide protection at all times. We are deeply grateful."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegrams National Government to Send Warships to Rescue Flood Victims 117

▲ Also Requests the Shipping Association to Assist

Recognizing the catastrophic flooding in Hankou, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the National Government and the Ministry of the Navy yesterday, requesting the immediate dispatch of warships to rescue flood victims. A letter was also sent to the Municipal Shipping Association, requesting assistance in arranging for ships to be sent for rescue efforts. The texts of the letters and telegrams are recorded below.

▲ Telegram to the National Government and the Ministry of the Navy: Recent reports indicate that the water level in Hankou has risen another four feet and two inches. If the water continues to rise, there are fears the entire city will be submerged. We request that all available warships be dispatched immediately to rescue flood victims. This concerns the lives of hundreds of thousands of people. We implore you to take swift action. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

▲ Letter to the Shipping Association: We are writing to inform you that recent reports indicate that the water level in Hankou has risen another four feet and two inches. If the water continues to rise, there are fears the entire city will be submerged soon. For the sake of rescuing flood victims, we request that your association immediately convene an emergency meeting to dispatch all available ships currently capable of navigating the Yangtze River, whether currently in port or due to arrive in Shanghai soon, to Hankou to provide emergency assistance. This concerns the lives of hundreds of thousands of people. We sincerely hope that your association will act decisively and swiftly.

Municipal Executive Committee Drafts Regulations for Public Servants to Donate Salaries for Flood Relief 118

▲ All Municipal Party and Government Agencies Should Implement

▲ Also Requests the Central Government to Organize National Relief Efforts

The Shanghai Special Municipality Party Department Executive Committee, noting the continuous rainfall causing disasters that have affected as many as sixteen provinces nationwide, with 500,000 displaced and destitute people in urgent need of relief, and recognizing that while flood relief committees have been established in various regions, Party and government officials should take the lead to set an example, has drafted five regulations for public servants to donate salaries for flood relief. These were submitted to and amended by the second standing committee meeting yesterday. The amended regulations are recorded below: (Regulations) (1) Committee members of this Party Department should each donate 30% of their August living expenses, staff with living expenses of 100 yuan or more should each donate 20%, and those with living expenses below 100 yuan should each donate 10%. Staff of district Party departments should each donate 10%. All donations will be advanced by the Municipal Party Department and deducted from the respective living expenses in three installments over three months. (2) This committee will instruct the standing committee members of district sub-branches to solicit donations from comrades as much as possible. Once a substantial amount is collected, it should be sent to this committee. (3) This committee will send letters to the Municipal Government, Garrison Headquarters, three court branches, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Office, Postal Administration, and the two railway administrations, requesting them to determine donation amounts with reference to Item 1 and instruct their subordinates to implement accordingly. (4) This committee will submit a report to the Central Government to circulate the above regulations to subordinate Party and government agencies for reference and urge them to develop effective methods for economic assistance regarding the flood disaster. (5) This committee will issue a public announcement to the people, encouraging all sectors to donate generously and contribute to this benevolent cause.

Pawnshop Public Welfare Association Solicits Donations from Pawnbrokers for Provincial Flood Disasters 120

The Shanghai Pawnbrokers Public Welfare Association convened a temporary board meeting on the 19th, attended by over ten people, chaired by Hu Jinzhang. After performing the required formalities, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that recent reports of flood conditions in various provinces were extremely serious, unprecedented in a century. Provinces such as Jiangsu, Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangxi were almost entirely flooded, with the disaster area extending across sixteen provinces. Not only was the harvest hopeless, but flood victims were displaced, and their suffering and imminent death were appalling. If relief efforts were not initiated immediately, millions of disaster victims would be drowned by the flood. The association's organization was premised on public welfare, so it was important to determine whether to appoint a committee to solicit donations for disaster relief. After discussion, it was resolved to actively conduct fundraising for disaster relief. The association appointed Wang Houchang, Weng Kangfu, Shen Tianjue, Qiu Bonian, Wang Xuanche, Zhu Yu, Hong Xiamin, Cao Pinfang, and Hu Jinzhang as a nine-member fundraising committee, authorized to begin in three groups on the 22nd to solicit donations from all staff members in the industry. It also printed pictorial and textual promotional materials and donation receipts. All collected donations were to be given to the Flood Disaster Emergency Relief Association and forwarded to the disaster areas for distribution. All printing, transportation, and meal expenses were to be borne by the association. A declaration was issued in advance to enable all sectors to jointly participate in this charitable act. A detailed account of expenses was prepared afterward and distributed to donors to demonstrate accountability.

Estimated Cotton Production for This Year 121

▲ Over 6.63 Million Piculs of Seed Cotton Produced

The China Cotton Industry Statistics Association released its first cotton production estimate for this year at 5:00 PM on August 20th. It estimates that cotton fields cover 34,438,068 mu, producing 6,631,501 piculs of seed cotton. This estimate is based on (1) reports from twelve provinces: Liaoning, Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang; (2) cotton crop conditions as of August 14th; (3) losses from floods affecting cotton crops in various provinces before August 14th have already been factored into the estimate.

British-Owned Public Bus Strike Yesterday 122

▲ Caused by Opposition to Employer's Dismissal of Workers

▲ Presented Nine Conditions for Improved Treatment

All 222 conductors of the British-owned China General Omnibus Company opposed the employer's dismissal of workers and demanded improved treatment. They went on strike yesterday morning, causing all bus routes to be completely suspended. To maintain transportation, the company assigned ticket inspectors to perform conductor duties and勉强[miǎn qiǎng] managed to operate routes 1, 2, and 9. As of last night, the matter remained unresolved. The authorities sent personnel to investigate. The various circumstances are detailed below.

▲ All Routes Suspended At 6:00 AM yesterday, the public buses of the Public Concession on Route 1 (Jing'an Temple to Park Shooting Range), Route 2 (Er Yangjing Bridge to Park Shooting Range), Route 3 (Zhoujiaqiao to Caojiadu), Route 5 (San Mao Ge Bridge to North Station), Route 6 (Tilanqiao to Park Shooting Range), Route 7 (Nanyang University to Caojiadu), Route 8 (Jing'an Temple to Tilanqiao), Route 9 (Jing'an Temple to Power Plant), and Route 10 (Caojiadu to Yinxiang Township), totaling 180 buses, were forced to suspend operations completely due to the conductor strike.

▲ Reasons for Strike At the end of July, the company summoned some representatives from last year's work stoppage for discussions and dismissed two Western employees, Pia and others, who had regularly oppressed workers. The workers were pleased upon hearing this. However, on the 10th of this month, the company dismissed ten conductors, citing embezzlement as the reason. The workers considered the dismissals unjustified and demanded reinstatement, but their request was denied. On the 18th, the company continued to dismiss six more conductors. All conductors were angered and, starting on the 19th, forty-four conductors did not report to work, implementing a slowdown. At 6:00 AM yesterday, all conductors went on strike to prompt the employer's awareness.

▲ Conditions Presented After the strike, the conductors convened a general meeting at 8:00 AM to discuss solutions. It was reportedly resolved in the meeting to (1) organize the Shanghai British-Owned Public Bus Workers Strike Committee; (2) elect twenty-one representatives to formally present the conditions to the company, totaling nine; (3) vow not to resume work until the objectives are achieved. The conditions are recorded below: (1) Drivers, ticket sellers, coppersmiths, laborers, bus cleaners, ticket writers, and ticket inspectors, regardless of seniority, shall receive a 30% wage increase, plus a housing allowance of 5 yuan and a rice allowance of 5 yuan. (2) Daily working hours shall not exceed eight hours, with four days of rest per month. Wages shall be paid as usual, and employees who have worked for one month shall receive four days of increased pay. (3) Wages shall be paid as usual during all holiday shutdowns, and those who work shall receive double pay. (4) Workers shall have the freedom to choose their own doctors, and medical expenses shall be borne by the company. Sick leave wages shall be paid as usual. (5) Workers shall have the freedom to organize clubs. The company shall subsidize 500 yuan per month for operating expenses and construct clubhouses. (6) Reinstate the workers dismissed after the 14th of this month and guarantee that no workers will be dismissed without just cause in the future. Dismissals must be approved by the club, and six months' severance pay must be provided after dismissal. (7) Skipping shifts shall not result in dismissal or wage deductions. (8) No red cards shall be issued. Sales amounts shall not be recorded in red ink. Tuition fees of 7.5 yuan and security deposits of 20 yuan shall be returned. (9) No workers who participated in this strike shall be dismissed, and wages shall be paid as usual during the strike period.

▲ Maintaining Transportation To maintain transportation, the company dispatched fourteen Route 1 buses from Jing'an Temple to Park Shooting Range and twenty Route 9 buses from Jing'an Temple to Power Plant at 8:40 AM, staffed by ticket inspectors as conductors. In the afternoon, six Route 2 buses from Er Yangjing Bridge to Park Shooting Range were also dispatched, also staffed by ticket inspectors as conductors.

▲ Authorities Investigate Ren Leping, the Sixth District Chief of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, upon learning of the bus conductor strike, immediately dispatched inspectors to investigate and sent patrol officers to maintain order in the vicinity. Upon receiving the report, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, recognizing the importance of transportation, sent Zhu Guilin to investigate the truth in detail for official handling.

▲ Refusal to Negotiate At 11:00 AM yesterday, the British-owned China General Omnibus Company convened a board meeting to discuss the conductor strike in detail. At 3:00 PM, the Public Bus Workers Strike Committee sent five representatives to the factory at 263 Connaught Road to present the nine conditions. However, the manager refused to receive them, and they were forced to withdraw. Upon hearing this, all workers were enraged and insisted on continuing the strike. It is reported that starting today, the drivers will also join the strike to provide assistance.

▲ Workers Express Views According to the Strike Committee yesterday, the company had only fifty buses when it first opened. Due to recent business growth, it has increased to 180 buses. Recently, it switched to diesel engines, doubling its profits. However, the conductors' treatment is quite harsh. Each person's monthly salary is only 20 yuan, with a maximum of 35 yuan. After various penalties, such as red cards (meaning conductors must get off the bus first and on the bus last at major stations, otherwise they are fined one yuan each time), the actual monthly wage is only 12 or 13 yuan, making it impossible to maintain a living. The company also arbitrarily dismisses workers and hires plainclothes ticket inspectors to monitor workers' actions. For example, conductor No. 259 was dismissed for embezzling four copper coins. In a matter of days, over ten people have been dismissed, so they were forced to take this action.

Murder of a Yarn Factory Inspector 126

▲ Two Victims Died Unjustly

Zhao Xilin, a Chanzhou native and inspector for the Yangshupu China First Knitting Factory, was ambushed yesterday morning in front of the Shenxin Ninth Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road. Numerous shots were fired, killing two people and injuring three others. The victim, Zhao Xilin, previously served as a detective in his hometown. It is reported that the ambush was due to past grievances. Details are as follows:

▲ Inspector Attacked Zhao Xilin, a native of Changzhou, is 32 years old. He has been working as an inspector at the China First Knitting Factory at 10 Longjiang Road for six or seven years. The Shenxin Ninth Yarn Factory at 89 Yangshupu Road opened this spring, and Zhao also joined that factory, concurrently serving as an inspector. Therefore, every morning when the two factories opened, Zhao would go to China First and then to Shenxin, as usual. At around 6:30 AM yesterday, Zhao was outside the Shenxin Ninth Factory after finishing his duties, talking with several fellow villagers on the road when suddenly seven or eight thugs wielding box cannons and iron rods approached. Upon seeing Zhao, they immediately opened fire, firing no fewer than one or two dozen shots. Zhao was unable to escape in time and was hit. His companions were also victims of collateral damage.

▲ Two Dead, Three Injured After the gunfire ceased, the thugs escaped during the confusion. It was found that a crab vendor had been fatally shot in the head by a stray bullet. Another victim, Li Litang, the owner of a nearby sesame cake shop, was shot in the temple and also died. Three people were injured and sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. They include Tao Ruisheng, a 30-year-old Changzhou native and worker at the Shenxin factory, who was shot in the buttocks; Xu Sihai, a 37-year-old Changzhou native and owner of the Yongxiangfeng Coffin Shop, who was injured in the right hand; and Xu Hexian, a worker at Shenxin, who was injured in the foot and is not in serious condition.

▲ Rooted in Grievances It is said that Zhao's shooting was due to past grievances. The Yangshupu police immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to apprehend the culprits. The two bodies were transported to the Pheron Road Mortuary for autopsy and will be reported to the court for inspection this morning. Zhao Xilin lived at 6 Anderli, Yangshupu Road, and had a wife and two concubines.

The Municipal Hall on Nanjing Road previously leased its premises to the China National Products Department Store. After the department store relocated, the building became dilapidated and no one renewed the lease. 金宗城's Suggestion to Use Yulan Festival Funds for Disaster Relief 129

Mr. Jin Zongcheng of the Shanghai Bank advocates using funds from the Yulan Sheng Hui (Ghost Festival) to aid disaster victims. He sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday stating: "Respected Editor, the current floods in various provinces of our country are causing severe devastation. Every time I read the newspapers, the scenes are so tragic that I cannot bear to finish reading. 'Relieving disasters and helping neighbors' is an ancient and clear teaching. Everyone has a sense of compassion. Although there are now various disaster relief associations raising donations, the disaster area is so vast that the more donations, the better. Being able to get just one more gold coin means saving one more life. Shanghai, during this seventh month of the lunar calendar, usually holds the Taiping Gong Jiao Yulan Sheng Hui. In my humble opinion, rather than relieving wandering souls, which involves superstition, it is better to prioritize the urgent and save the dying in the disaster areas. This merit is even greater than building a seven-story pagoda."

▲ All-Day Revenue from Food and Beverage Department

▲ Donated to the Provincial Flood Relief Emergency Association

Guanshengyuan Food Company on Nanjing Road in this port, moved by the floods and disasters in various parts of the country, with tens of millions of victims in urgent need of relief, and acting on the principle of human mutual assistance, has initiated a disaster relief effort. Tragic Accident of German Ship Colliding with Dredging Boat 132

▲ Negotiating Compensation Issues

After the Hai Long dredging boat of the Dredging Bureau was sunk by the German ship "Kaibaierenshi" in the Chenjiazhui section of the Huangpu River on Tuesday morning, the Tokyo Salvage Company and Ruirong have sent people underwater to investigate whether it can be salvaged, in order to report to the chief engineer of the bureau for a decision. The boat is currently sunk at the bottom of the river, 30 feet deep, right in the navigation channel, posing a danger to large ships entering and exiting. As for the bodies of the three drowned crew members, two were found on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, and the other was found in the evening. The night watchman Zhou Ansheng, who was on the deck at the time, saw the perilous situation and jumped down, desperately shouting for help, hoping to alert the entire crew to escape. Unexpectedly, he lost his footing and fell into the steam cylinder, where he was scalded to death by boiling water. The Dredging Bureau originally planned to ask the local security guard Qin Bingqing to report Zhou Ansheng's body to the Wusong Seventh District First Precinct, and then request the local court for an autopsy. However, due to an order from the River and Lake Department, to facilitate negotiations with the German ship for compensation, the body was sent to the Feilun Road autopsy center to await examination by the First Special District Court. Therefore, it was not until yesterday morning that the autopsy was completed and the burial arranged. Zhou Ansheng's family went to the Dredging Bureau yesterday morning to meet with the chief engineer, arguing that Ansheng did not die in the water but was scalded to death after falling into the steam cylinder while trying to save the lives of the entire crew, which was a truly tragic and unbearable sight. Moreover, Ansheng left behind a meager estate and many dependents, so they requested generous compensation and requested for a coffin and clothing. The engineer of the bureau replied that according to the regulations of the bureau, only two years' salary would be given to the bereaved family in case of death in the line of duty. However, in this case, Ansheng died after being scalded due to panic after falling into the steam cylinder while trying to save the lives of the entire crew, so the tragic situation was understandable. Whether or not an exception should be made for generous compensation would have to be decided by a bureau meeting. Thereupon, Ansheng's wife and children thanked him tearfully and withdrew.

Chinese Tram Conductor Beaten 133

▲ Because a Worker Refused to Pay for Damages

The Route 1 Changlu tram of the China Tram Company left Xiaodongmen for Gaochangmiao at 6:45 yesterday morning. More than ten workers from a certain place were getting on the tram at Xiaodongmen Station. One of them accidentally broke a piece of the tram window glass while boarding. The conductor asked him to pay for the damage, but the worker refused, leading to a conflict. Later, a police officer was called, and they went to the First District General Office together. After questioning and judging by the director, the worker was ordered to pay four jiao of foreign currency to settle the case. Unexpectedly, the worker was not satisfied and gathered a group of people to wait at Xuejiabang. When the tram passed by, they made things difficult for the conductor No. 98, dragged him off the tram, and beat him up, injuring his back and waist. Later, the ticket inspector caught a glimpse of the scene and sent conductor No. 98 to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. At that time, tram traffic in the area was suspended for forty minutes.

Operating an Advertising Company 135

▲ Do Not Use the Company Name Without Authorization

Advertising businesses in this city generally use the name "company." Recently, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau stated that advertising businesses using the word "company" must comply with the "Provisional Regulations on Company Registration" and supplementary measures promulgated by the Central Government in December of the 17th year of the Republic (1928) and register first; otherwise, they may not use the word "company" without authorization. It is reported that the Public Utilities Bureau has been instructed by letter to order all advertising companies to register with the Social Affairs Bureau according to law within one month of receiving the document; otherwise, they should change the company name to comply with the law.

Continued Trial of the Dancer Dung-Throwing Case 137

▲ Ge Chongxi Denies Instigation

▲ Sun Ai'ying's Arm Develops Blisters

Sun Ai'ying, a dancer from Shanghai Dance Hall and a native of Nanjing, was riding in a rickshaw at 10:10 p.m. on the 12th of this month, passing through the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Mahuo Road, when Zhou Fugen, Qiu Genfa, and Ye Zixiang suddenly stopped her and poured dung on her head. Sun called the police, who arrested Zhou and the other two and handed them over to the First Special Court for interrogation. They confessed that Ge Chongxi of the Paris Dance Hall was suspected of instigating the attack. The court ordered a postponement to summon Ge to court for further questioning. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Gongliang held a continued trial. Ge Chongxi and his legal representative Jiang Baoli attended the court to await questioning. Sun Ai'ying also hired lawyer Zhang Zirang to represent her. First, Lawyer Zhang stated that because the plaintiff was insulted by the three defendants, blisters had developed on her arm, which had now grown large. Moreover, at the time, an embroidered scarf and a jade brooch were robbed, so the plaintiff accused the three defendants of the crimes of insult, injury, and robbery. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, rose and stated that the case had already been publicly prosecuted by the police. If the plaintiff wanted to file another lawsuit, she would have to file a private prosecution and could not include it in this case. Ge Chongxi had already been summoned to court today, but the police had not filed a lawsuit. Whether or not to file a lawsuit in the future was still under consideration. However, the case was being tried by Cheng Shangfeng. Should the trial be updated today? He requested a ruling. Judge Jiang then instructed that the trial be updated. Sun Ai'ying then recounted the situation at that time. Judge Jiang then questioned the three defendants who instigated them. They replied that Zhou Degong instigated them. He asked if Ge Chongxi instigated them. They replied no. Judge Jiang then instructed Sun Ai'ying to go to the forensic doctor to examine the wounds on her arm. The plaintiff's lawyer, Zhang, also stated that since the police did not prosecute Ge Chongxi, the plaintiff should file a private prosecution separately. Lawyer Jiang Baoli also stated that when the plaintiff was questioned in court last time, she accused Ge Chongxi of molestation, which damaged Ge's reputation, so he must also file a counterclaim, etc. Judge Jiang then summoned Ge to stand in the witness box. Ge said that the plaintiff's contract with him had not expired when she joined Dahai. Because she was a woman, he did not deal with her. Now, this happened suddenly, and she falsely accused him of instigation, which he did not understand. Judge Jiang said that further investigation of the case was still necessary, so he ordered a postponement for further questioning.

Robbers in Hongzhen North Shoot and Wound the Victim Who Resists 138

▲ The Victim, Zhao Shicai, is in Critical Condition

Zhao Shicai, a 51-year-old resident of Zhujiawan Village in Hongzhen North, supports himself by cultivating garden plots. He is diligent and frugal and has saved a little money. As a result, they only robbed a few silver dollars, as well as copper coins, which were very few in number. Chen Liqing, a young woman from Suzhou, also known as Sha Chen, married Sha Xiangyu, an actor from Tianjin, in the 13th year of the Republic (1924) through a matchmaker. Cement Wall Crushes Two Workers to Death 141

Xinrongji Construction Factory is currently constructing a five-story building for the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society on Aimaiyuxian Road in the French Concession. At noon yesterday, five workers were washing their faces and eating lunch in the shade in the northeast corner when a section of cement wall made of wooden boards on the fifth floor collapsed due to dryness, crushing the heads of plasterers Guo Binglong and Chen Xinghe, causing their brains to burst. Workers Xu Changhui, Xu Fazi, and Wang Ageng suffered broken hands and feet. After the Western police learned of the incident, they reported it to the police station and sent the injured to Guangci Hospital. Guo Binglong died of serious injuries after being admitted to the hospital. The hospital notified the police, who sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for autopsy, pending a court examination.

Shooting and Resistance to Arrest Case Occurs on Caoxi Road 142

▲ Two People Arrested One After Another

Deng Zhiming, a police officer from the Second Post of the Sixth District Third Precinct of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, Zhang Jinshan, a police officer from the Third Post, and Du Futang, the squad leader, were patrolling on Caoxi Road around 4 a.m. yesterday when they saw a hooded car (Municipal License No. 4429, Rental License No. 17554) coming from the north. As Officer Zhang and others were stepping forward to stop it, three people suddenly jumped out of the car and fired handguns directly at the police. Officer Du and others immediately drew their guns and returned fire. Both sides fired seven or eight shots in a row, but no one was injured. At that time, the car immediately turned around and sped north, and the three robbers who got out of the car also disappeared. After hearing the gunshots, Director Liu Lun and Inspector Chuan Xinggeng led the police to the scene and searched with Officer Du and others. However, because it was dark and the area was remote, the robbers managed to escape. They returned to the station and used the telephone to notify the Longhua Branch and the Sixth District Second Precinct, requesting them to assist in the search. Later, Zhou Yida, the police chief of the Tushanwan Police Station, led police officers Ding Yuelou, Liu Jintai, and Fan Yuansheng to arrest Mao Jusheng, a local resident, in the reeds south of the Shuntong Guild Hall on Xietu Road. At 8 a.m. yesterday, the French police sent Xie Amao. After Director Liu Lun briefly interrogated them, he ordered them to be temporarily detained. How the shooting occurred will be investigated and reported later.

Investigation of the Maid's Private Escape 146

▲ Buying a Maid is Also a Crime

Zhang Tang, a local woman residing in a bungalow in Baijiazai, Gelan Road, purchased Cui Zhen, the eight-year-old daughter of Mao Panxing from Tongzhou, for 68 foreign dollars through Yang Qiqiao on April 3 of this year. However, at around 1 p.m. the day before yesterday, Zhang Tang instructed Cui Zhen to go out and fetch water, but she did not return. Later, it was learned that Cui Zhen had been taken back and hidden by her father, Mao Panxing. The Yangshupu Police Station was notified, and Chinese detective Pan Yulin was sent to arrest Mao Panxing, Yang Qiqiao, and Yang Qiqiao. However, Cui Zhen's whereabouts were still unknown. They were taken to the police station, and a copy of Cui Zhen's sales contract was found at Zhang Tang's home, stating that Cui Zhen was a maid. The police chief believed that she was also committing a crime by buying another person's daughter to enslave her. He ordered them to be detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to the police lawyer Li Zhishan's statement of the case, Cui Zhen's brother Lin Gen, 13 years old, testified that because his family was poor, his father received 68 foreign dollars and sold Cui Zhen to Zhang Tang as a daughter. He did not know anything else. Zhang Tang testified that Yang Qiqiao was the intermediary and purchased Cui Zhen as an adopted daughter, not as a servant, and hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend her. The defendant, Mao Panxing, was conspiring with Yang Qiqiao to release the pigeons (deceive her), and her lawyer wanted to file a complaint, requesting that they be released on bail to await interrogation. Mao Panxing testified that he did not admit to hiding his daughter, and Yang Qiqiao testified that he was indeed the intermediary when Cui Zhen was sold to Zhang Tang as a daughter. This was a mutual agreement, so he did not receive any brokerage fees. He asked for consideration. After Judge Shen Bingle examined the testimony, he ordered Mao and Yang to be returned to custody, and Zhang Tang was allowed to post a substantial shop guarantee. The case was adjourned for further investigation.

Girl Pushed Against a Plank Corner 147

▲ Died from Her Injuries

Jiang Er'nan, the nine-year-old daughter of Jiang Bao, a woman residing at No. 96 De'an Lane, North Shanxi Road, Wuxi, was standing in the doorway to cool off at around 10 p.m. the day before yesterday. Zhang A'xiao, a girl living in the same residence, went out to fetch water and returned home. When she reached the door, she asked Jiang to move aside, but Jiang refused. She then pushed Jiang. At that time, Hu Chuanbing, a 13-year-old boy from No. 78 in the same neighborhood, was also there and accidentally bumped into Hu. Hu then pushed Jiang, causing her head to hit the corner of the washboard, causing a severe injury. Jiang's mother took the girl to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but because the injury was critical, she soon died. The hospital notified the Huishan Police Station to send detectives to investigate. The girl's body was taken to the Feilun Road Autopsy Center. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court was notified, and Prosecutor Guo Huaipu arrived at the office for examination. According to Zhang A'xiao's testimony, she was carrying hot water and was afraid of scalding Jiang, so she pulled her away. Hu Chuanbing testified that Jiang stepped on his foot and hurt him, so he pushed her, but did not expect her to fall and be injured. After reviewing the testimony, Judge Guo ruled that the girl Jiang Er'nan died as a result of being pushed and injured by Hu Chuanbing, and ordered the mother to provide a coffin and clothing for the body.

The Maritime Surveying Bureau Will Take Over the Customs Surveying Affairs 150

▲ The Waterway from Wusong to Jiangyin

▲ Warning Ships Still Issued by the Customs

Hua Dong News Agency reports that the waterway survey from Wusong to Jiangyin has been handled by the Jianghai Customs. The Ministry of the Navy believes that since the Ministry of the Sea has established a Maritime Surveying Bureau, matters related to waterway surveying should be transferred to the Bureau. Previously, it had submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, earnestly requesting that the section of the waterway be transferred to the Maritime Surveying Bureau first. The Bureau received a training order from the Executive Yuan forwarded by the Navy yesterday, and will send personnel to take over. The Executive Yuan's training order is recorded below for compliance. It is reported that the Ministry of Finance stated that the Ministry of the Navy had requested that the surveying affairs of the section between Wusong and Jiangyin be transferred to the Navy Surveying Bureau and that warning ships be issued. It is approved that the Surveying Bureau is fully responsible for the surveying affairs of this section and can be assigned to handle it. However, regarding river and other engineering matters, the Customs should be allowed to accurately set up buoys and other objects in the section to maintain safety so that there will be no obstruction. If the Executive Yuan approves, please order the Ministry of Military Affairs to comply with the aforementioned method. The Ministry will instruct the relevant departments to remove their responsibilities for the surveying affairs of that section. As for the Ministry of the Navy's original request for the issuance of warning ships, the issuance of warning ships is uniformly issued by the Customs nationwide and is of great importance to navigation safety. It should be handled by a single agency to avoid disputes. The Ministry should reserve this section. The Ministry of the Navy's request to transfer the surveying affairs of the section between Wusong and Jiangyin to the Maritime Surveying Bureau is hereby submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and instructions for implementation. Therefore, it is reported that the Ministry has repeatedly submitted requests to the Executive Yuan for review and handling. In addition to instructing that the report be acknowledged, it is stated that the request to transfer the surveying affairs of the section between Wusong and Jiangyin to the Maritime Surveying Bureau is the same as the request of the Ministry of the Navy. Please order the Ministry to instruct the relevant departments to take over. In the future, regarding changes in rivers and other matters, the Bureau must immediately notify the Maritime Patrol Engineering Department of the surveying situation and news so that buoys and other objects can be moved. Also, the warning signs should still be uniformly issued by the Customs nationwide to avoid disputes, as this is to maintain navigation safety. It should be approved and ordered to the Ministry of the Navy to comply. This order.

Yangtze River Shipping Increases Prices Due to Flooding 156

▲ Refusing to Load Goods Except for Grain and Essential Supplies

▲ Uniform 10% Surcharge Above Jiujiang

The Yangtze River region has been hit by flooding, with Wuhan being the most severely affected, followed by Jiujiang and Chongqing. The flooding has persisted for a month without receding and is continuing to rise. Shipping companies in Shanghai received a telegram from Wuhan yesterday, stating that the water level had risen several more inches, reaching a depth of 57 feet at its deepest point. The Jardine Matheson Wharf has also risen to 55 feet and 3 inches, making it difficult for ships to load cargo onto the docks. Dockworkers above Jiujiang have successively raised their wages, placing a heavy burden on the shipping companies. Therefore, six companies in Shanghai—China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Jardine Matheson, Butterfield & Swire, Sanpei, Ningshao, and Nisshin—held a meeting at Jardine Matheson yesterday afternoon. They decided that, starting immediately, they would refuse to load cargo destined for Wuhan except for grain and essential supplies, as well as cargo that passengers cannot pick up themselves at the ship, to avoid stockpiling in the warehouses. It was also decided that, starting on Monday, the 24th, they would uniformly add a 10% surcharge to the original freight rates for shipments from Shanghai to Jiujiang and Hankou, as well as from Hankou to Yuezhou, Changsha, and Xiangtan, to compensate for the losses. This decision has been communicated to the customs brokers.

Labor Dispute on the Taizhou Steamer 157

▲ Conflict Between Waiters and Purser

Zhou Yixiu, a waiter on the Taizhou Steamer of the Wenzhou-Taizhou Line Taizhou Company, began working on the ship in 1928. According to company regulations, he was required to pay a deposit of 200 silver dollars. Zhou, being unable to pay the full amount at once, paid 100 silver dollars in July of that year, and another 100 silver dollars the following year. Both payments were handled by the purser, Chi Zhushu. However, the purser neglected to forward the payments to the company. Last month, during a company investigation of deposits, it was discovered that Zhou Yixiu had been working for a long time without paying the deposit, and his name was not on file with the company. As a result, he was dismissed. After learning of this, the waiter went to the company to explain that he had already paid the deposit to the purser. The purser was questioned by the company and, on the return trip from Taizhou to Shanghai, returned 200 silver dollars to Zhou on the 19th, ordering him to leave the ship upon arrival in Shanghai. Zhou protested and was beaten and had a shirt torn. Also, last Saturday, when the ship was sailing from Shanghai to Haimen, a box of woolen cloth (containing 40 bolts) was loaded in the main cargo hold. On Monday morning, after arriving in Haimen, it was discovered that 36 bolts of woolen cloth, valued at 656 silver dollars, were missing. The company was notified upon the return to Shanghai, and the shareholders decided that the purser, the accountant, the cargo handler, and the six watchmen would be held responsible for the loss. The purser told the waiters that if they were unwilling to compensate for the loss, they would be suspended from work. The waiters argued that, according to regulations, the watchmen were responsible for missing cargo on the deck, but they were not responsible for cargo lost within the hold. They felt oppressed by the purser and reported the matter to the Shanghai Branch of the Seamen's Union yesterday, requesting assistance.

Wang Yansong Resigns from Anti-Japanese Association 158

Wang Yansong, Standing Committee Member and Director of the Custody Section of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee, sent a letter to the City Party Headquarters and the Anti-Japanese Association yesterday, resigning from all positions held concurrently in the association. The original letter reads: "Respected Sirs, since the Japanese government instigated Korean nationals to persecute Chinese, causing a tragic incident, righteous indignation has swelled up across the country, and a struggle has been launched. Representatives from all sectors of this city convened a meeting and resolved to organize the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee, using the method of permanent economic severance with Japan as a tool to wage a life-or-death battle against Japanese imperialism. I, Yansong, was erroneously elected as a committee member and was further elected to the Standing Committee, responsible for custody. In terms of ability, I am certainly insufficient to undertake such an important task. In terms of public justice, I dare not simply abandon my duty. I have tried my best, exerting my limited abilities and striving to follow the cause. Moreover, because the military campaign to suppress bandits is currently in progress, there is no shortage of people taking advantage of the situation. How can we demonstrate a spirit of unity against external enemies? How can we avoid providing ammunition for our enemies to use? I have racked my brains, earnestly concerned and actively working. My humble private feelings cannot be expressed in words. Considering that I am physically weak and the task is arduous, I dare not shirk the toil of serving against external enemies, even if I fail. However, if in addition to external work, I am forced to cope with difficult environments and to navigate avoidable disputes, it will only waste my energy and contribute nothing. I am deeply pained and unable to cope. Therefore, I have no choice but to resign from the positions of committee member and Standing Committee Member and Director of the Custody Section of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee. As for the anti-Japanese movement, as long as I have breath, my determination will not waver. As a citizen, a party member, and a merchant, I have responsibilities to fulfill and will certainly make the necessary efforts. I will not be negligent simply because I have resigned as a committee member. I am sending this special letter to respectfully inform you and humbly request your review and approval. This is my earnest prayer."

Directorate General of Telecommunications Standardizes Telegram Translation Fees 159

▲ One Cent Per Word Regardless of Urgency

The Directorate General of Telecommunications issued an order to its branch offices yesterday, stating: "According to instructions from the Ministry of Communications, the charges for translation services at various telegraph offices vary, with some charging a percentage of the telegraph fee and others charging one cent per word. The methods are inconsistent. Furthermore, it is inappropriate to charge a percentage of the telegraph fee for the translation of urgent telegrams and telegrams requiring verification. It is now stipulated that, starting immediately, for all telegrams that require the sending office to translate them into code, a uniform translation fee of one silver cent per word shall be charged to ensure consistency. In addition to this separate order, you are hereby instructed to comply and to instruct all subordinates to comply with this order."

Careless Fire in a Shantytown on Gonghe New Road 161

On the south side of Taiyang Temple Road on Gonghe New Road in Zhabei, there is a vacant lot of approximately three mu, surrounded by about thirty shanties built from iron sheets. The residents, numbering no fewer than fifty households, are mostly laborers and pig farmers. At around 11:00 AM yesterday, a fire broke out in the home of a Yang family from Yancheng due to careless cooking. The fire quickly spread to the pile of firewood, and flames raged out of control. Within half an hour, the thirty-odd shanties were reduced to ashes. Fire brigades from various sections of the city rushed to the scene and made strenuous efforts to prevent the fire from spreading to the Zhifu West Lane and Fude Bathhouse on the north side. These buildings sustained only minor damage, such as scorched windows and doors. Most of the residents were away at work when the fire broke out. By the time they returned, they had no homes to go to. Their cries of despair were pitiful. Fortunately, the fire occurred during the day and no one was injured. The Yang family, who started the fire, was arrested by the police from the Fourth District and taken for investigation. It is reported that about one hundred pigs, both large and small, were burned to death.

Shanghai Silk Industry Cooperative Opens 163

Huasha Town, Shaoxing, has always been a silk-producing area, with an annual output of 300,000 bolts. In recent years, due to sluggish sales abroad and frequent natural disasters and wars at home, weaving has suffered, and merchants have only focused on profits. As a result, business has declined drastically, and workers have lost their jobs. To remedy the situation, Hu Jitang and others invited silk merchants and weaving workshops to organize the Shanghai Silk Industry Cooperative, aiming to mutually research and improve products and conduct sales with integrity. The cooperative opened last month. Its distribution center is located at No. 1260 Zhongde Lane, Beijing Road, Shanghai. It is said that various merchants have praised the cooperative for its genuine goods and fair prices. Recently, to expand business and facilitate customers, a retail department and a mail-order department have been added. Whether purchasing whole bolts or individual cuts, the prices are the same as wholesale prices. The cooperative's dedication to service is a boon to buyers.

News from Various Labor Unions 174

▲ Shanghai Publishing Industry Union: The Shanghai Publishing Industry Union issued a public notice to the members of the Zhonghua Book Company yesterday, which was filled with resentment. Excerpts are as follows: "To all members of the Zhonghua Book Company, your General Manager Lu Feikui has repeatedly undermined your labor union. You have all experienced his tactics and will never forget them. Since you joined our union, Lu Feikui has been panicked and lost his composure. The leaflet he issued yesterday (August 12) was his final lament. We have told you in detail about the history, evolution, and status of the Publishing Industry Union when you joined the union, but we will briefly explain it again. Our union was reorganized and established according to the orders of the party and government on February 28 of this year. Before February 28, it was indeed called the Commercial Press Union, but it took several struggles to reach its present state. During the first strike in 1925, 80% of the workers at the Commercial Press earned less than 25 yuan. After seven years of long-term struggle, the average salary has now reached 47 yuan, which is enough to live a normal life. Comrades, humans can only survive through struggle. If the workers at the Commercial Press had not had the spirit of long-term struggle, their lives would certainly be as difficult as yours are today. On the day of our union's founding meeting, Mr. Zhu Jiahua, a member of the Central Committee, personally attended and gave guidance. He highly praised the spirit of our union and urged us to expand the number of members and to bring all unorganized publishing workers in the city into the union. Comrades, the status of our union is one of the best not only in Shanghai but also in China, and it deserves the attention of society. The reasons for our union's recruitment of members are two: (1) The apparent reason: After the promulgation of the Labor Union Law, according to Article 6 of the Labor Union Law, 'Only one labor union can be established for workers of the same occupation or industry in the same area.' The factory labor union can no longer exist. The Shanghai Publishing Industry Union was born in response to this situation. The workers of the Commercial Press have a history of seven years of organization, which is rare in the publishing industry. Of course, they were the first to join. Because the workers of other publishing houses had not joined at the time of our union's representative meeting on February 28, there was no way to elect them as directors or supervisors. After Lu Feikui sees February 28 next year, any member of our union from any company will have the right to elect and be elected. At that time, after the workers of the Zhonghua Book Company are elected as directors and supervisors, Lu Feikui should stop talking nonsense about '...luring others to join...' (2) The real reason: The capitalists of the publishing industry can unite with various publishers to form the Book Industry Trade Association. The workers of the publishing industry can unite and join the union, which is also a special right granted by law. The Publishing Industry Union should show a spirit of fearlessness and liberate the fellow workers who are being oppressed by the iron-fisted capitalists and let them live as 'human beings.' The purpose is very clear. This time, Lu Feikui, knowing that the strength of the Publishing Industry Union cannot be insulted and that it is not as easy to destroy as the Zhonghua Book Company Union, had to deceive the City Chamber of Commerce, the Book Industry Trade Association, and the Color Printing Industry Trade Association to act as shields, sending out a telegram and publishing advertisements. He exhausted all his tricks, but he could not pull out a single hair of the Publishing Industry Union. On the contrary, he aroused the anger of all labor unions in the city, who issued a joint declaration that they must eliminate this public enemy, Lu Feikui. The conditions for improving treatment that were passed at the founding meeting of the Zhonghua Book Company Office are mostly those that have been implemented in the industry for several years. Every article is legal and reasonable. Lu Feikui said that it was laughable, but hopefully he won't laugh and then cry. He said that Article 9, the profit-sharing method, is 'even more laughable,' which shows that he is an incorrigibly stubborn old man. The members of the labor union, which is based on the Three Principles of the People, all advocate for cooperation between labor and capital. On the one hand, they seek to improve the living conditions of workers, and on the other hand, they seek to increase productivity and make the shareholders not suffer losses from the increased profits. This profit-sharing system can not only reconcile the conflict between labor and capital, but also improve the productivity of employees. With a capital of 2 million yuan, the Zhonghua Book Company can easily make a profit of 300,000 to 400,000 yuan if the management is proper. Why should Lu Feikui be so alarmed? Comrades, if you do not want to live an inhuman life under Lu Feikui's constant oppression, then is there any other way out other than to strengthen your solidarity under the banner of the Publishing Industry Union? Comrades, our union leads more than 4,000 members, who are your direct backing. All the labor unions in the city, leading 800,000 workers, are your indirect backing. Your support is so strong. Comrades, move forward! The final victory will belong to you!"

▲ Postal Workers Union: On August 19, the Postal Workers Union held its 35th Executive Committee meeting, chaired by Xiao Qingshan. The reported items were omitted. Discussion items: (1) The new organizational law of the General Post Office is difficult to implement. How should it be remedied? Motion for a decision. Resolution: (A) It was decided to hold a joint meeting of the two unions at 2:00 PM this Saturday to thoroughly discuss the matter. (B) To handle the matter in accordance with the resolutions of the 29th meeting. (2) The Chengdu Postal Workers Union sent a telegram stating that the price of rice has risen to 60 yuan per picul and requesting the union to ask the authorities for rice subsidies. How should this be handled? Motion for discussion. Resolution: Submit the request to the General Labor Union for approval. The union will strongly support the request. (3) The 32nd branch submitted a request to be given a copy of the newspaper. Motion for discussion. Resolution: Reply by letter. (4) The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union sent a letter recommending Kang Yong, Ge Fei, Lao Jieming, and other seven people as members of the preparatory committee for the 2nd Sports Meet. Please set a date for the joint meeting to discuss all matters. Resolution: Zhu Xuefan, Zhang Kechang, and Qi Jiamou are responsible for handling the matter. The meeting was adjourned.

(1) The outstanding issue of the labor-capital treatment contract dispute of the union has been submitted to the Central Party Headquarters and the Executive Yuan of the National Government for approval. Motion for a decision. Resolution, notify the workers of each factory branch to participate in the patriotic movement, boycott Japanese goods, and purchase domestic goods. The first and second branches will raise donations separately to help overseas Chinese in Korea. Vote, passed. The rest were omitted.
