Words of Wisdom 178

— Holding Buddha

When joy comes, check yourself. When anger comes, check yourself. When laziness comes, check yourself. When recklessness comes, check yourself. Then there will be no faults.

▲ As seductive as a nine-tailed fox, as eloquent as a mockingbird, as fierce as a three-legged tiger, as venomous as a two-headed snake. Today's modern woman seems to possess all these traits.

▲ The taste of love is like cherry blossom candy: soft and sweet, but sometimes there are dregs, making it as bland as maltose.

▲ Governing a country is easy, governing a wife and children is difficult, and governing a woman is even more difficult.

▲ When the fire of love is ignited, the flower of life blooms profusely. When the fire of desire is ignited, the root of life is immediately burned.

▲ It is a common ailment of today's students to prefer falling behind on the battlefield to falling behind in the field of love.

▲ A shrew is like osteomyelitis, a termagant is like cholera, and a modern woman is like meningitis.

▲ The warbling of an oriole is lovely; weeping softly is even more lovely. Lengthy and verbose speech is detestable. Babbling is cute; the sound of reading is even more endearing. Sniveling is loathsome.

▲ The Japanese call the Chinese people's boycott of Japanese goods a "childhood disease." I call the Japanese people's brutal behavior "hydrophobia."

Recording Qing Daoren's Threatening and Fraudulent Marvelous Writings 179

— Zhang Shanzi

My late teacher, Li Meian of Linchuan, also known as Qing Daoren, lived in seclusion by the sea after the 1911 Revolution, making a living by selling writings and calligraphy. His noble character and profound knowledge were universally respected and need no further elaboration. This year marks the 65th anniversary of his birth, and his former colleagues from the Li clan are celebrating by collecting and publishing his various poems and writings. They also plan to place advertisements in newspapers seeking contributions. I possess several exquisite letters from my late teacher that are unknown to the world. I am recording one here to demonstrate his noble spirit and integrity, which is evident in everything he did. His letter in response to the Weiliang Association states: To the esteemed gentlemen of the Weiliang Association, I, the poor Daoist, am a heartbroken man. During the national upheaval of 1911, I sought death but could not find it. I drifted to the sea and made a living by selling my writings. My impoverished household consists of nearly forty people, who depend on my brush for their sustenance. For six years, I have been in dire straits. I received a letter from your association, to which I have already responded. I recently received another letter stating that since I have not obtained access to the thoroughfare for ten thousand people, how can I prevent people from taking what they want? It also stated that I should prepare a remittance of three hundred dollars to HSBC to assist your association. This is a misunderstanding. I am a seller of writings, not someone who has a large sum of money stored in a chest. There are days when I earn a few dollars, and days when I don't earn a single dollar. This type of business does not thrive unless the market is peaceful. Only then do people think about such embellishments. It is not like a pheasant that can be caught everywhere. Recently, credit has been tight, and for more than ten days, I have not had a single dollar of income. I can barely take care of myself. How can I help your association? As the saying goes, "If you have money, money is your security; if you don't have money, your life is your security." Moreover, people who love life must have hope for the future. I have no wife, no concubines, no children. All my children are my brothers' children or the grandchildren of widows. My friend Wu Jianqiu said, "The Daoist has no wife or concubines to support, yet he has the burden of a family." Moreover, the world is changing daily, and treacherous and evil people are all in high positions, possessing heavy armies. The disaster of national subjugation is imminent. I only seek a quick death and great liberation. I received two letters, so I sincerely inform you of this. Please conduct a thorough investigation. If there are any lies, I will willingly accept being led to a firing squad with guns and bombs, and I will have no regrets. Qing Daoren bows his head. This letter was written by his family member. The original manuscript was retained. My tenth brother, Junshou, purchased and treasured it at a high price. (Requital)

Discovery of Primitive Villages in Germany 180

— Shoulin

In primitive times, humans lived in caves or built nests in treetops, both in the East and West. Later, as culture gradually developed, they began to have houses and formed villages. However, their lives at that time were quite simple. Recently, German archaeologists discovered a village constructed by humans during the Stone Age in Lindenthal, near Cologne. This village was constructed over five thousand years ago. Its construction is completely identical to that of the Middle Ages. The village is surrounded by a moat, about seven feet deep and sixteen feet wide. Several feet away from the moat is a fence made of stacked firewood. Beneath the moat, many fragments of broken pottery were found. There are also dozens of well-preserved house foundations. However, the construction methods are chaotic and unsystematic, with no overall system. In terms of appearance, they are curved. The holes around the wooden fence prove that the houses were entirely constructed of wood. In some places, there are long, narrow cracks in the ground, perhaps used by the inhabitants to cool food. In addition, several rectangular open spaces were found, one of which was more than seventy feet long. There are many wooden pillars on top, but no household items, which shows that their lives at that time were simple. The most numerous items discovered this time are pottery. In addition, a large number of Stone Age human tools, such as hand grinders, flint knives, arrowheads, hand axes, and tools made of animal bones, were found. It is said that the archaeologists plan to transport all of these items to the Berlin Museum for display for the reference of the country's people.

Recording Two Tragic Cases 181

— Jing Mengdie

The conscription of laborers by the police is a cruel policy unique to military times. In particular, the implementation of this policy in rural areas has caused unrest. Often, not even the chickens and dogs are spared, reminiscent of the scenes in Du Fu's "The Officer at Stone Moat." Last month, I returned to my hometown on business. At that time, the war situation in Jiangxi was urgent, and there was a conscription of laborers in the countryside. About seven or eight miles from my home, in a place bordering Dantan, there was a tailor who was walking alone in the fields. He was forced by the police to run wildly across a bridge, but there were several police officers waiting to intercept him under the bridge. He stopped and pleaded, "If you must not spare me, then take me from the water." The police ignored him and surrounded him from both sides. In desperation, the tailor jumped into the river. The rushing water swept away this unfortunate soul, joining the company of river spirits. The police then swaggered away, claiming that they were following orders from above and had no choice. It is said that the tailor was from Yancheng, making a living in Jiangnan due to poverty. He was in his thirties, with elderly parents and young children at home.

▲ A New Bride Saves Her Husband and Kills a Thief. The world is deteriorating. During this summer season, burglaries in the countryside have become frequent, not waiting for the end of winter. After my return, within a week, there were three burglary cases within a few miles, all with the same cruel methods: placing the homeowner on a cauldron and setting it on fire. In a small village, a farmer recently married a husband surnamed Zhou. Zhou was diligent and thrifty, and had accumulated a small amount of savings after many years of work. Not long after marrying into the family, he was targeted by thieves. About seven or eight people conspired and broke into the house. It was midnight. The wife woke up and quickly woke her still-sleeping husband, telling him to escape quickly. She then stood guard at the bedroom door, holding two sickles, which were farm tools. Fortunately, the thieves had no firearms, and only carried knives and clubs. The wife was strong and powerful, wielding the two sickles like mandarin duck swords. The thieves could not enter the room. They retreated out the door, and the wife pursued them, fighting the thieves in the courtyard. The thieves surrounded her from all sides, and knives and clubs rained down. The wife was wounded on the forehead, and blood covered her face, but she became even more enraged. She struck down one thief with force, severing his arm, and he fell to the ground and died. The others were also wounded and scattered like birds and beasts. At dawn, the ground was covered in blood. People said that Zhou was spared the tragedy of being burned alive thanks to the wife's strength. For a woman to rely on farm tools to defeat a group of thieves, how brave is that! However, her determination to save her husband was the cause.

Random Musings from Jie Lu 182

— Cheng

In a certain city, continuous rain caused a disaster. Thousands of refugees had nowhere to go. The mayor, distressed and worried, said to the representatives of the citizens, "I have been worried about the flood since dawn. I am currently convening a meeting to discuss relief efforts, but I am suffering from a lack of funds..." Before he could finish speaking, a red invitation card from his lover arrived, inviting him to keep their date at the theater last night.

A certain gentleman, in the name of saving the country through education, tirelessly founded a private school. Once completed, he opened the door wide, recruiting wealthy but uneducated children. With his purse full, the gentleman then turned his attention elsewhere.

A certain county commissioner stood on a podium, delivering grand speeches to the masses about eradicating corrupt officials. His left hand was in his suit pocket, tightly gripping the bribe money from the compromise sale of opium.

Travel Notes on India (86) 184

— Linghua

Since reading the history of India, observing its social organization, and participating in various social activities, I have come to understand the lives of people outside of China. Seeing the way the Indian people support their religious leader Gandhi, I now understand that the so-called Brahminism (here, using Buddhist scriptures with a slight hint of contempt) is not to be underestimated in its content, which is roughly similar to Buddhism. Let us compare and discuss it. Among the world's religions, those east of India include Confucianism, Buddhism, and Daoism. Those west of India include Islam, Christianity, and Hinduism. There are now six factions. If we add the old imperial capitalism and the newly emerging Russian Marxism, they are also known as the eight major factions. Religion is discussed, but politics is also included. First, China is the religion of the Principle of the People's Livelihood. Since Confucius's emphasis on the people's welfare, the "July Fire Flow" and "September Clothing Distribution" of the Three Dynasties, the "Filial Piety and Diligence in Farming" of the Han Dynasty, and the "Farming and Reading" of the Song and Ming Dynasties all reflect this. It is not related to religion. The tenets of this religion are not favored by the Indian people. Daoist philosophy is far inferior to that of India and is not an enemy of the Indian people. Buddhism, on the other hand, lacks ethical and economic organization and does not emphasize deities. It has been defeated by Hinduism and driven out of all of India. (This is what the Indian people say.) The three religions of China are not enemies of Hinduism. Islam, backed by military force, once ruled India, but the result was a great failure. It is not worth the Indian people's attention and cannot govern India. Christianity lacks philosophy. In the view of the Indian people, it is not worthy of study. Therefore, the two religions, Islam and Christianity, have failed in Hinduism after hundreds of years of experimentation, even when supported by political power. These five major religions of the world are not enemies of Hinduism. Hinduism is now being widely disseminated in the Americas. A new Buddha, Gandhi, has emerged with great fanfare, causing a great stir. The Indian people worship Gandhi, calling him a god and Buddha, even more so than the Chinese worship Sun Yat-sen and the Americans worship Washington. Moreover, the Indian people's love for their wives, the wives' love for their husbands, and the children's love for their mothers all contain divine meaning. They call their mothers goddesses. They extend this to cows and their entire families, as they provide milk. Therefore, they call cows great mothers. From this perspective, the Indian people are also deeply emotional. In short, none of the world's five religions can shake Hinduism, which has been tested for thousands of years.

However, in the future, two major factions will emerge that will challenge Hinduism. What will happen then? One is imperial capitalism, and the other is Russian communism. First, imperial capitalism. The Indian religious leader Gandhi uses only a coarse cloth filial piety hat and robe to resist it. (It is indeed the item used by the Chinese in mourning.) The British lose 600 million yuan a year, which means that the foundation of the empire is already shaken. It is also not enough to control the Indian people's lives. However, Russianism is greatly admired by young people. It may be a problem in the future. However, I observe that Gandhi's followers originally came from Tolstoy-like ideologies. Many have also studied in Russia. Even if Russia is able to invade India southward, India will definitely not become a swallowed and digested Russified nation. In my opinion, the three organizations of politics, economics, and society in India in the future must create a new system between Tolstoy and Marx. Brahmanism. I used to despise it when I read Buddhist scriptures. Now I know that it is a copper wall and iron bastion, having survived after grinding and competing with various ideologies of the world.

Woman, Woman (25) 185

— Yao Sufeng

Thus, the conflict between the two parties began. Like a rabid dog unleashing its bestial nature, this was Xiao Rong. Xiao Rong completely forgot that the woman lying on the ground was his wife. He only saw her as an enemy destroying his career. But Xiao Rong's wife deeply remembered that he was her husband, the only son of her father-in-law and mother-in-law, the light of her hope. But now he was conquered by anger, and the deception had stung her deeply. Amidst the ever-changing emotions, everything lost the harmony that should exist between a couple.

Miss Ding saw Xiao Rong's cruel actions for the first time. Besides sighing for herself and pitying others, she could not bear it.

"Mr. Lu! I think... you shouldn't be making such a scene here. Why don't you go back to Suzhou to talk? But you should also know that although women in the world are weak, they may always have a chance for revenge!" She always spoke in this cold and sarcastic tone.

Xiao Rong's flames of anger seemed to have been fueled by humiliation. He had been venting everything on his wife. Suddenly, he forcefully dragged his wife, disregarding everything, all the way from upstairs to downstairs, and then out the door. Although Qiu Zi was pulling him and Miss Ding was trying to stop him, everything failed, and they could only tolerate the further development of this tragedy as much as possible.

The rain was falling even harder. The raindrops did not know people's pain, and they attacked the earth relentlessly. The thunder was like beating war drums, and the lightning was like igniting guiding torches. The dark clouds and violent wind further highlighted the tension of the moment. Xiao Rong was like a madman, no, more like a mad dog, unaware of all of this. He opened the door of the Ding family's house, and even such heavy rain did not reduce his advancing anger. Xiao Rong's wife was crying and wailing, being dragged on the ground by Xiao Rong. Her tears almost turned into blood, her voice was hoarse, and her strength was exhausted. No one was able to stop her husband's violence.

The Money Market Turns Tight Again 190

▲ Foreign Exchange Remains the Same

▲ Market Overview Yesterday in the market, the position of silver dollars and foreign exchange remained largely unchanged. However, a certain bank and money shop suffered huge losses, slightly affecting their counterparts. As a result, the money market tightened slightly, especially for bank overnight loans, which became particularly expensive. As for formal commercial needs, they remained moderate, with no signs of special prosperity.

▲ Exchange Rates "Foreign Exchange" In both the morning and afternoon markets, supply and demand were balanced, so the market price did not fluctuate, remaining at 7 mace, 2 fen, 5 li and a half. This was similar to the morning market the day before. "Silver Exchange" was 1 mace, 1 fen in the morning market, initially 1 mace, 4 fen in the afternoon market, closing at 1 mace, 2 fen. The bank's listed rate was 4 fen. The rate for overnight loans suddenly tightened, with a market rate of 1 mace, 6 or 7 fen.

▲ Subsidiary Coin Market Situation The Jiangnan small foreign coins were 6 mace, 5 fen in both the morning and afternoon markets, with no difference from the previous day. 4,000 jiao were traded in the morning market and 2,000 jiao in the afternoon market. The Guangdong small foreign coins were 6 mace, 4 fen, 4 li and a half in the morning market, and 8 mace, 4 fen, 4 li, 3 hao and 7 hu and a half in the afternoon market. 130,000 jiao were traded in the morning market and 70,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Copper coins suddenly decreased by 2,000, to 375,000 wen.

▲ Silver Dollar Inflow and Outflow "Silver Funds" Yesterday's bank receipts included over 2.3 million in Chinese merchant receipts, 1.5 to 1.6 million in foreign merchant receipts, 9.56 million in various freight, tax and miscellaneous receipts, over 2 million in special receipts, and 1.2 million in warehouse receipts. Japanese banks received over 3.6 million in various receipts, over 900,000 in special receipts, and 500,000 in warehouse receipts. Money shops and silver firms received over 62 million in receipts due to the 20th comparison period, over 4.2 million in overnight loan receipts, over 1.2 million in various remittance receipts, and over 1 million in cash withdrawals. "Foreign Funds" 1.42 million in foreign exchange remittances were made in the morning market and 1.36 million in the afternoon market. 55,000 in banknotes were made in the morning market and 35,000 in the afternoon market. 185,000 in off-market banknotes were made in the morning market and 85,000 in the afternoon market. Inter-bank trading was 750,000 in the morning market and 600,000 in the afternoon market. Over 1.3 million in foreign account transactions were received and disbursed among banks, over 1.9 million in foreign overnight loans were received, over 12 million in foreign public money shop receipts, over 1.9 million in foreign loan borrowing, over 500,000 in small money shop transactions, and over 300,000 in customer source transactions.

The Shanghai Financial Community's Concerns About Lending to Hankou 191

The Shanghai financial community has always had significant financial and commercial exchanges with Hankou, relying on the circulation of goods and the turnover of funds. This time, the entire Hankou area has been flooded, commercial activities have been suspended, and a thriving commercial port has become a watery country. There is no possibility of financial exchanges. According to surveys, the amount lent to Hankou, both fixed-term and non-fixed-term, is no less than five or six million. Although the end of the year is still far away, time flies, and it will arrive in a blink of an eye. It is unknown whether it can be repaid. According to the hopes of people in the Shanghai financial community, they would feel very fortunate if half of it could be recovered. This shows the difficulty of doing business in Hankou.

Yarn and Cotton Market Turns Flat from Decline 193

The yarn market fell in the morning and flattened in the afternoon, with a still weak trend. Due to the slump in the world cotton market, Three Goods Yarn has been falling sharply for days, causing panic. Speculators continued to emerge, but a certain large short seller slightly covered their positions, with some going near and some going far. Although new sellers made some offerings, they were all absorbed by the large short sellers, so the market did not appear extremely weak. Actual sales in the market were more active, with the Sichuan and Yunnan gangs purchasing more of 10-count coarse yarn. Confidence slightly strengthened. Due to a certain manufacturer's assessment of strong actual demand, they have been controlling the yarn market this month, with a strong trend of purchasing goods. Driven by this, the far months may temporarily fluctuate between 52 and 53 taels.

▲ Human Biao Did Not See Major Weakness The Human Biao market opened with continuous declines in American cotton, leading to weak sentiment. After falling by one or two taels each, large players bought in aggressively, strengthening the market. As a result, each month fell by five, six, seven, or eight qian. In the afternoon, news of good spot prices caused a rebound of three, four, or five qian, with the current month rising by one tael. Transactions totaled 44,650 bales. The Cotton Market Shows No Sign of Improvement 194

The cotton market slightly declined, with a still weak trend. Most cotton merchants in the local area are inclined to buy in, because the flood situation in Hankou is rising and not receding, and the harvest from all routes may not be good. Therefore, the intention to go long is very strong. However, the world cotton market is in a state of no return, and new low prices are gradually being discovered. There are also many large players who are aggressively shorting. The spot price of American cotton, Mitterling, is calculated to be close to 30 taels in Chinese currency, only equivalent to 29 taels and 7 qian. The local cotton mills have no intention of inquiring, while foreign firms and foreign companies are selling actively in the market. The prices are said to be particularly negotiable. As for the manufacturers, they are all watching the world trend and not taking action.

▲ Han Biao Fell by Three Qian The Exchange's Han Biao market opened, following the decline in American cotton, sentiment was still flat, with each month falling slightly by two and a half qian to one and a half qian. First Estimate of Cotton Production in Local Area 195

The China Cotton Industry Statistics' first estimate of cotton production this year was released at 5:00 PM on August 20th. It estimates 34,438,068 mu of cotton fields and 6,631,501 dan of seed cotton production. This estimate is based on reports from the twelve provinces of Liaoning, Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, using the cotton crop situation before August 14th as the standard. The losses caused by floods to cotton crops in various provinces before August 14th have already been included in the calculation.

Wheat Futures Are Weary and Tending to Loosen 199

▲ The Spot Goods Are Rare and Steady

Yesterday, the wheat market was generally flat and tired. Although the domestic floods swept the country and the price of grain was bound to soar, there was still no way to deal with the foreign surplus. Now that the disaster in our country is getting worse, the US government has re-proposed a large number of wheat loans to our country. In recent days, this matter may become a reality, so many bulls outside the industry are inevitably shocked. Those with weak minds have gradually come out, and the market has gradually become loose. As a result, this month is two points smaller than the previous day, September is three points smaller, October is one point smaller, and November to January are two points smaller. The spot wheat is not rich in arrival, and they are all thinking about selling, and the price is steady. Kunshan, Liuhe, Penglai, and Pudong opened more than 1,000 packages, which were handled by Fuxin Huafeng.

Long-Term Flour Mills Are Constantly Selling 200

Yesterday, the flour market generally showed a tired trend. Although the foreign wheat was slightly better by about one angle, the actual sales were not good, and there were many floating sales outside the industry. Because American wheat will have a large number of loans to China, the market can be optimistic in the future. A certain large factory has a very rich stock, and the long-term also has a daily output, which has also reached more than 100,000 packages yesterday. The whole day's market was relatively clear, but the market atmosphere was not strong. As a result, August and September were two and a half cents smaller than the previous day, October was seven and a half cents smaller, November was five cents smaller, and December and January were one point and two and a half cents smaller.

Milan's silk factories suspended work due to summer holidays, and the sales of cocoons were stagnant. In addition, Russian cocoons were sold, and the price of cocoons fell sharply. Recently, silk factories have started work after the holidays and started to purchase raw materials separately. The price of cocoons has soared. The price of spring dried cocoons is 91 lira per kilo, and the price of summer dried cocoons is 78 lira, each rising by four or five lira.

Social News

Marshal Foch's Diary of the European War 231

— Translated by Gu Angruo

(A) North of the Somme River, the British Third Army advances towards the direction of Bapaume and Polong.

(B) East of the Scarpe River, the French Tenth Army advances towards the roads of Schenies and Scheniesayason.

I added the following sentences at the end of the letter:

The French army has achieved such results with independent attacks. It can be seen that this offensive will be more promising if it is extended to both wings.

Since July 15th, the enemy army has driven no fewer than 120 divisions to the front lines. Our army has now reached a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. With such achievements, we should make further efforts to achieve complete success. The above-mentioned attacks should be carried out as soon as possible. Success or failure depends on this.

On the afternoon of August 12th, I met Marshal Haig and Commander Petain near Aye. They and I were being received by the King of England. They expressed their complete agreement with the military order just mentioned. Our army will begin a series of fierce attacks to implement the new plan. (To be continued)
